    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1206953573783437323 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/13/2024 8:22 AM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02132024-822-am .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1206953573783437323 message-timestamp-1206953573783437323"}

    ::: {#message-content-1206953573783437323 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    For some reason I am obsessed with the idea that more people should
    be empowered to use web technology to do stuff. and as a guy who
    spent most of his life in (documentary) linguistics, the stuff I
    always found myself working was stuff related, mostly, to
    documentation and revitalization. So stuff like building
    dictionaries, learning tools, interactive text interfaces, stuff
    like that.
    :::
    :::

    ::: {#message-accessories-1206953573783437323 .container_dbadf5}

    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .groupStart__56db5 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1206957273532858408" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1206957273532858408 uid_1 message-content-1206957273532858408 uid_2 message-timestamp-1206957273532858408"}

    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1206957273532858408 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/13/2024 8:37 AM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02132024-837-am .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1206957273532858408 message-timestamp-1206957273532858408"}

    ::: {#message-content-1206957273532858408 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    I've also been a web guy forever, so naturally all the stuff I built
    was on the web. But here's the thing: it's not obvious what "on the
    web" means. There are many things that you might say are "on the
    web", but the way that they are actually on the web and the ways
    that they get there can vary wildly.
    :::
    :::

    ::: {#message-accessories-1206957273532858408 .container_dbadf5}

    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .groupStart__56db5 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207411658335461396" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207411658335461396 uid_1 message-content-1207411658335461396 message-accessories-1207411658335461396 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207411658335461396"}

    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1207411658335461396 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/14/2024 2:42 PM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02142024-242-pm .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1207411658335461396 message-timestamp-1207411658335461396"}

    ::: {#message-content-1207411658335461396 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![üï∏Ô∏è](/assets/f62ee53f93a6d4c9f807.svg){.emoji aria-label="üï∏Ô∏è"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":spider_web:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} Here's what I get when I open the file in my browser.
    Take a look at the URL in the address bar, it's a bit weird:
    `file:///Users/me/sample-words.txt`{.inline} First off, most URLs do
    not start with `file`{.inline}, they start with `http`{.inline} or
    `https`{.inline}. This is because opening a file in the way we have
    here (Right click \> `Open with‚Ä¶`{.inline}) opens the file from the
    file system in the same way you might with a word processing program
    like Word, or any other desktop application. This matters a lot, as
    it turns out, but we will come back to this issue. For now, opening
    files this way is enough to mess let us mess around with a web page.
    Which we will now do.
    :::
    :::

    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*2:45 PM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614 .timestamp_cdbd93
    .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207412321165643827 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![üï∏Ô∏è](/assets/f62ee53f93a6d4c9f807.svg){.emoji aria-label="üï∏Ô∏è"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":spider_web:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} Proof: go to the directory where your
    `sample-words.txt`{.inline} file is saved, and dupilicate it. (On
    Mac that will result in a file called
    `sample-words copy.txt`{.inline}. Rename that file to
    `sample-words.html`{.inline}. Now open *that* in the browser just
    like you did before.

23. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207412879272181801}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207412879272181801" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207411658335461396 uid_1 message-content-1207412879272181801 message-accessories-1207412879272181801 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207412879272181801"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*2:47 PM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614 .timestamp_cdbd93
    .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207412879272181801 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![üï∏Ô∏è](/assets/f62ee53f93a6d4c9f807.svg){.emoji aria-label="üï∏Ô∏è"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":spider_web:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} Note that there might be some weirdness when you
    change the file suffix. A Mac, for instance, throws the message
    above. The default application for a `.txt`{.inline} file is a text
    editor, whereas the default application for an `.html`{.inline} file
    is whatever your default browser is. It's find to say
    `Use .html`{.inline} here. Then double-click the resulting file, or
    else use `Right click -> Open with‚Ä¶`{.inline} and choose a browser.
    (Same difference.)
    :::

24. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207414341805023262}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .groupStart__56db5 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207414341805023262" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207414341805023262 uid_1 message-content-1207414341805023262 message-accessories-1207414341805023262 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207414341805023262"}

    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1207414341805023262 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/14/2024 2:53 PM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02142024-253-pm .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1207414341805023262 message-timestamp-1207414341805023262"}

    ::: {#message-content-1207414341805023262 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![üï∏Ô∏è](/assets/f62ee53f93a6d4c9f807.svg){.emoji aria-label="üï∏Ô∏è"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":spider_web:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} Okay, now what? Well, you will see one of two things,
    depending on some rather mysterious variables. One possibility is
    that you will see something like the image on the left, where all
    the Coptic words and definitions have been merged onto a single
    line, but they look okay. (More on that wrapping in a second.) The
    more crazy [![ü§Ø](/assets/e8513d5385138a93db22.svg){.emoji
    aria-label="ü§Ø" draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":exploding_head:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} result is the one on the right, which I got when I
    opened the file with Safari instead of Firefox. WTF. This, my
    friends, is to do with Unicode. If you're a language nerd learning
    web stuff, you have to think about Unicode *right away*. A lot of
    web tutorials out there might not help you with this, so we're going
    to make sure we get it right.
    [[(edited)]{.edited_b20dd9}]{.timestamp_cdbd93}

25. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207415369275547658}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207415369275547658" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207414341805023262 uid_1 message-content-1207415369275547658 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207415369275547658" aria-describedby="uid_3 message-reactions-1207415369275547658"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*2:57 PM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614 .timestamp_cdbd93
    .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207415369275547658 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![üï∏Ô∏è](/assets/f62ee53f93a6d4c9f807.svg){.emoji aria-label="üï∏Ô∏è"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":spider_web:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} What's happening here is that one the browsers
    (Safari) isn't configured to use Unicode by default. It might be the
    case that I could go into the preferences and tell Safari to always
    assume Unicode, but that would only solve the problem for me
    ---¬†ultimately we're going to want to put this stuff on the web, and
    we hardly want to ask users to go fiddling with browser settings in
    order to see a few words in Coptic! The bottom line here is that we
    can modify our `HTML`{.inline} file (`sample-words.html`{.inline})
    to tell the browser "Hey, browser! This file is in Unicode!
    Interpret it as such!"
    :::
    :::

26. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207416047024476220}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207416047024476220" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207414341805023262 uid_1 message-content-1207416047024476220 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207416047024476220"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*3:00 PM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614 .timestamp_cdbd93
    .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207416047024476220 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![üï∏Ô∏è](/assets/f62ee53f93a6d4c9f807.svg){.emoji aria-label="üï∏Ô∏è"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":spider_web:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} It's worth pausing here to reflect on what's going on:
    1.  The browser reads the contents of a file (usually an
        `.html`{.inline} file)
    2.  The browser processes that content and then displays it

    It's step 2 that matters. *Many magical things* go on in step 2,
    magical things that can give you magical superpowers that can help
    you to create magical things and share them with the world. For the
    last couple of steps today, we're going to:
    1.  Fix our `HTML`{.inline} file (it's not valid right now!)
    2.  Fix it so we're sure our browser interprets our file as Unicode.
    :::
    :::

    ::: {#message-accessories-1207416047024476220 .container_dbadf5}
    :::
    :::

27. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207419071742742548}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .groupStart__56db5 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207419071742742548" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207419071742742548 uid_1 message-content-1207419071742742548 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207419071742742548"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    
    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1207419071742742548 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/14/2024 3:12 PM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02142024-312-pm .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1207419071742742548 message-timestamp-1207419071742742548"}

    ::: {#message-content-1207419071742742548 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![üï∏Ô∏è](/assets/f62ee53f93a6d4c9f807.svg){.emoji aria-label="üï∏Ô∏è"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":spider_web:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} So as we have seen, an `HTML`{.inline} file is just a
    `.txt`{.inline} file with an `.html`{.inline} suffix. But that's not
    all there is to it: the contents of an `HTML`{.inline} file must
    also obey the rules of how an `HTML`{.inline} file should be
    written. `HTML`{.inline} is a [*markup
    language*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markup_language "markup language

    (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markup_language)"){.anchor_c8ddc0
    .anchorUnderlineOnHover__78236 rel="noreferrer noopener"
    target="_blank" role="button" tabindex="0"}, which means that it
    contains not only text content, but also "meta" content that tells
    the browser how to interpret the various bits of content and to
    treat them specially. `HTML`{.inline}, as I'm sure you know, uses
    `<tag>`{.inline}s to mark up content. In fact, the entirely to an
    `HTML`{.inline} file is wrapped in a tag called, astonishingly
    enough, `<html>`{.inline}. Note that `<html>`{.inline} is called an
    "opening" tag, and it has a matching "closing" tag:
    `</html>`{.inline}:
    ### sample-words-2.html

        <html>
        ‚≤°‚≤ô‚≤ü‚≤ü‚≤© ‚Äòwater‚Äô
        ‚≤°‚≤è‚≤ì ‚Äòhouse‚Äô
        ‚≤°‚≤£‚≤Å‚≤õ ‚Äòname‚Äô
        ‚≤ß‚≤£ÃÖ‚≤£‚≤± ‚Äòqueen‚Äô
        œ©‚≤Å ‚Äòunder‚Äô
        ‚≤°‚≤±‚≤õ‚≤â ‚Äòstone‚Äô
        ‚≤°œ©‚≤Å‚≤ì ‚Äòhusband‚Äô
        ‚≤°‚≤õ‚≤ü‚≤©‚≤É ‚Äògold‚Äô
        ‚≤ß‚≤ô‚≤Å‚≤Å‚≤© ‚Äòmother‚Äô
        ‚≤Å‚≤õ ‚Äònot‚Äô
        </html>
    :::
    :::

    ::: {#message-accessories-1207419071742742548 .container_dbadf5}
    :::
    :::
    :::

28. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207421775563202680}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .groupStart__56db5 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207421775563202680" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207421775563202680 uid_1 message-content-1207421775563202680 message-accessories-1207421775563202680 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207421775563202680"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    
    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1207421775563202680 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/14/2024 3:23 PM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02142024-323-pm .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1207421775563202680 message-timestamp-1207421775563202680"}

    ::: {#message-content-1207421775563202680 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![üï∏Ô∏è](/assets/f62ee53f93a6d4c9f807.svg){.emoji aria-label="üï∏Ô∏è"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":spider_web:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} We still haven't fixed our problem in Safari. And in
    fact, adding that tag didn't seem to do much at all. Let's fix that
    now. In fact, for an `HTML`{.inline} file to be valid, it needs a
    bit more structure.
    1.  A `<!doctype html>`{.inline} This always has to be the first
        line in an `HTML`{.inline} file. Note the weird `!`{.inline},
        the fact that there are *two* words in there,
        `doctype `{.inline} and `html`{.inline}, and the fact that it
        doesn't have a matching closing tag. Of course the first tag is
        going to be weird.
        [![üòë](/assets/edb192589e9e0f05f91b.svg){.emoji aria-label="üòë"
        draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
        data-name=":expressionless:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
        .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false"
        role="button" tabindex="0"}
    2.  `<head>`{.inline} and `<body>`{.inline} tags. If you leave these
        out, the browser will figure it out, but you shuoldn\'t, because
        it's a useful way to distinguish document metadata and the
        content of the page itself. Basically, anything which is inside
        the `<body>`{.inline} tag is what the browser will display to
        the user.
    3.  A `<title>`{.inline} - The title is what shows up in the tab
        (which will otherwise show the document's URL). It goes inside
        the `<head>`{.inline} tag.
    4.  `<meta charset=utf-8>`{.inline} Oh boy. This one's weird. Like
        `<title>`{.inline}, it goes inside the `<head>`{.inline} tag.
        (Another weirdo tag which doesn't have a matching close tag.)
        Believe it or not, this thing means that the page is in Unicode.
        This will fix the Safari problem above.

    So there you go, a workable starting point for creating valid
    `HTML`{.inline} pages. Here's the whole thing that you can try:
        <!doctype html>
        <html>
        <head>
          <title>A few Coptic words</title>
          <meta charset=utf-8>
        </head>
        <body>
        ‚≤°‚≤ô‚≤ü‚≤ü‚≤© ‚Äòwater‚Äô
        ‚≤°‚≤è‚≤ì ‚Äòhouse‚Äô
        ‚≤°‚≤£‚≤Å‚≤õ ‚Äòname‚Äô
        ‚≤ß‚≤£ÃÖ‚≤£‚≤± ‚Äòqueen‚Äô
        œ©‚≤Å ‚Äòunder‚Äô
        ‚≤°‚≤±‚≤õ‚≤â ‚Äòstone‚Äô
        ‚≤°œ©‚≤Å‚≤ì ‚Äòhusband‚Äô
        ‚≤°‚≤õ‚≤ü‚≤©‚≤É ‚Äògold‚Äô
        ‚≤ß‚≤ô‚≤Å‚≤Å‚≤© ‚Äòmother‚Äô
        ‚≤Å‚≤õ ‚Äònot‚Äô
        </body>
        </html>

    [[(edited)]{.edited_b20dd9}]{.timestamp_cdbd93}

32. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207709243873034320}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207709243873034320" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207708824153096232 uid_1 message-content-1207709243873034320 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207709243873034320"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*10:25 AM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614
    .timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207709243873034320 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    ## [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì" draggable="false" data-type="emoji" data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804 .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"} Let's learn about `HTML`{.inline} markup: separating content and presentation

    Today's topic will be shorter because I have just a little time. We
    will just carry out one task:
    1.  Learn a few tags to make the page from
        [![üï∏Ô∏è](/assets/f62ee53f93a6d4c9f807.svg){.emoji aria-label="üï∏Ô∏è"
        draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
        data-name=":spider_web:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
        .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false"
        role="button" tabindex="0"}yesterday look like a word list.

    [[(edited)]{.edited_b20dd9}]{.timestamp_cdbd93}
    :::
    :::

    ::: {#message-accessories-1207709243873034320 .container_dbadf5}
    :::
    :::
    :::

33. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207710279589306448}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207710279589306448" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207708824153096232 uid_1 message-content-1207710279589306448 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207710279589306448"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*10:29 AM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614
    .timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207710279589306448 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} Why an axe? Well, as we have seen, the text in an
    `HTML`{.inline} page is "chopped up" into pieces by adding tags like
    `<head>`{.inline} and `<body>`{.inline}. Most of the tags we learned
    yesterday were "about" the structure of the page as a whole ---
    remember, you don't *see* content inside the `<head>`{.inline} in
    the main browser window (although you do see the content of the
    `<title>`{.inline} tag inside the page's tab). That stuff is
    metadata. (The weird `<!doctype html>`{.inline} tag that you just
    have to have to create an `HTML`{.inline} page, the
    `<meta charset=utf-8>`{.inline} that says "this page is in Unicode",
    and then top level `<html>`{.inline} tag that wraps everything
    (*except* the `<!doctype html>`{.inline}), which (always!) has two
    "children" (directly nested) tags, `<head>`{.inline} and
    `<body>`{.inline}.
    :::
    :::

    ::: {#message-accessories-1207710279589306448 .container_dbadf5}
    :::
    :::
    :::

34. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207711500848861225}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .groupStart__56db5 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207711500848861225" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207711500848861225 uid_1 message-content-1207711500848861225 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207711500848861225"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    
    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1207711500848861225 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/15/2024 10:34 AM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02152024-1034-am .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1207711500848861225 message-timestamp-1207711500848861225"}

    ::: {#message-content-1207711500848861225 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} Today we're just going to look at the contents of the
    `<body>`{.inline} tag. Recall that our wordlist had all run onto a
    single line. Why? It's important to understand the reason ---¬†recall
    that the browser "reads" and "interprets" the content of the page
    it's rendering. When we opened a `.txt`{.inline} version of the
    wordlist, the lines remained intact. But when we converted it to
    `HTML`{.inline}, we saw the "line collapse".
    :::
    :::

    ::: {#message-accessories-1207711500848861225 .container_dbadf5}
    :::
    :::
    :::

    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207711576824746014" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207711500848861225 uid_1 message-content-1207711576824746014 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207711576824746014"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*10:34 AM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614
    .timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207711576824746014 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    ## [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì" draggable="false" data-type="emoji" data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804 .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"} In `HTML`{.inline} whitespace characters collapse into a single space.

36. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207712354972991488}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207712354972991488" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207711500848861225 uid_1 message-content-1207712354972991488 message-accessories-1207712354972991488 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207712354972991488"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*10:37 AM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614
    .timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207712354972991488 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    This is true of *all* whitespace, not just line breaks. If you go
    into your wordlist, and add a bunch of spaces between ‚≤°‚≤ô‚≤ü‚≤ü‚≤© and
    'water', when the browser renders them, you will just see one space,
    as shown in the attached image:
        <!doctype html>
        <html>
        <head>
          <title>A few Coptic words</title>
          <meta charset=utf-8>
        </head>
        <body>
        ‚≤°‚≤ô‚≤ü‚≤ü‚≤©                                     ‚Äòwater‚Äô
        </body>
        </html>

37. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207713113445503056}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207713113445503056" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207711500848861225 uid_1 message-content-1207713113445503056 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207713113445503056"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*10:40 AM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614
    .timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207713113445503056 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} Again, keep in mind that the purpose of
    `HTML`{.inline} is to *describe the structure of web content*, not
    to control its presentation directly. It's not that we *can't*
    control presentation¬†--- the contrary, we can control presentation
    with *incredible* precision and flexibility¬†---¬†it's just that
    content and presentation are *separate concerns*.
    :::

    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1207714632077418586 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/15/2024 10:46 AM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02152024-1046-am .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1207714632077418586 message-timestamp-1207714632077418586"}

    tabindex="0"} Now, this idea of [separation of content from
    presentation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_content_and_presentation "separation of content from presentation

    (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_content_and_presentation)"){.anchor_c8ddc0

    [contentious](https://alistapart.com/article/separation/ "contentious

40. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207715516660326411}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207715516660326411" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207714632077418586 uid_1 message-content-1207715516660326411 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207715516660326411"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*10:50 AM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614
    .timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207715516660326411 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} Different tags serve to distinguish different kinds of
    content, and learning `HTML`{.inline} is in large part learning what
    kind of tags are appropriate (Note: not "correct") for the content
    you're marking up. It's interesting to think about how many "things"
    there are in our wordlist, I can think of at least these:
    1.  word
    2.  definition
    3.  wordlist
    4.  language
    :::

    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .groupStart__56db5 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207733260508205187" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207733260508205187 uid_1 message-content-1207733260508205187 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207733260508205187"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    
    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1207733260508205187 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/15/2024 12:00 PM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02152024-1200-pm .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1207733260508205187 message-timestamp-1207733260508205187"}

    ::: {#message-content-1207733260508205187 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} So what kind of markup would we use to make our
    wordlist 1) look better and 2) "mean better"? There are a lot of
    `HTML`{.inline} tags ([132 as of last
    count](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTML/Element "132 as of last count

    (https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTML/Element)"){.anchor_c8ddc0
    .anchorUnderlineOnHover__78236 rel="noreferrer noopener"
    target="_blank" role="button" tabindex="0"}), so how do you know
    which ones to use?

43. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207733958721413153}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207733958721413153" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207733260508205187 uid_1 message-content-1207733958721413153 message-accessories-1207733958721413153 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207733958721413153"}

    [*\[*12:03 PM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614

    ::: {#message-content-1207733958721413153 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} here, we'll use the `<p>`{.inline} tag, which means
    "paragraph". Unsurprisingly, each paragraph gets its own line:
        <!doctype html>
        <html>
        <head>
          <title>A few Coptic words</title>
          <meta charset=utf-8>
        </head>
        <body>
        <p>‚≤°‚≤ô‚≤ü‚≤ü‚≤© ‚Äòwater‚Äô</p>
        <p>‚≤°‚≤è‚≤ì ‚Äòhouse‚Äô</p>
        <p>‚≤°‚≤£‚≤Å‚≤õ ‚Äòname‚Äô</p>
        <p>‚≤ß‚≤£ÃÖ‚≤£‚≤± ‚Äòqueen‚Äô</p>
        <p>œ©‚≤Å ‚Äòunder‚Äô</p>
        <p>‚≤°‚≤±‚≤õ‚≤â ‚Äòstone‚Äô</p>
        <p>‚≤°œ©‚≤Å‚≤ì ‚Äòhusband‚Äô</p>
        <p>‚≤°‚≤õ‚≤ü‚≤©‚≤É ‚Äògold‚Äô</p>
        <p>‚≤ß‚≤ô‚≤Å‚≤Å‚≤© ‚Äòmother‚Äô</p>
        <p>‚≤Å‚≤õ ‚Äònot‚Äô</p>
        </body>
        </html>

44. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207734409222951062}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207734409222951062" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207733260508205187 uid_1 message-content-1207734409222951062 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207734409222951062"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*12:05 PM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614
    .timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207734409222951062 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} This is pretty good. At least things look more
    readable. However, note that while we have marked up each
    word/definition pair in a `<p>`{.inline} tag, there are several
    things that are only implicit here: There is no tag that corresponds
    to the wordlist *as a whole* (this might seem abstract, more about
    this later). Furthermore, there are no tags that correspond to
    Coptic words versus (English) definitions. Let's tackle that second
    problem first, in the next version.
    [[(edited)]{.edited_b20dd9}]{.timestamp_cdbd93}
    :::
    :::

    ::: {#message-accessories-1207734409222951062 .container_dbadf5}

45. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207742614330155040}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .groupStart__56db5 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207742614330155040" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207742614330155040 uid_1 message-content-1207742614330155040 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207742614330155040"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    
    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1207742614330155040 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/15/2024 12:37 PM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02152024-1237-pm .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1207742614330155040 message-timestamp-1207742614330155040"}

    ::: {#message-content-1207742614330155040 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} Now we're going to complexify things and give separate
    tags for each (Coptic) word and each (English) definition. As it
    happens, you're not supposed to nest *p* tags inside of each other
    (for "reasons", for now), so you wouldn't want to do this:
    [![üîï](/assets/194741b4a90752cc9615.svg){.emoji aria-label="üîï"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":no_bell:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} don't do this
    [![üîï](/assets/194741b4a90752cc9615.svg){.emoji aria-label="üîï"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":no_bell:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"}
        <p>
          <p>‚≤°‚≤ô‚≤ü‚≤ü‚≤©</p>
          <p>‚Äòwater‚Äô</p>
        </p>

    [[(edited)]{.edited_b20dd9}]{.timestamp_cdbd93}

46. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207744358095388672}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207744358095388672" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207742614330155040 uid_1 message-content-1207744358095388672 message-accessories-1207744358095388672 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207744358095388672"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*12:44 PM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614
    .timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207744358095388672 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} Instead, we should nest some other kind of tag. There
    is a very "generic" tag `<span>`{.inline} which basically means
    "this text deserves its own tag for some unspecified reason", which
    will do for now. Both the word and its definition can go in a span.
    Here's the whole page and a screenshot:
        <!doctype html>
        <html>

        <head>
          <title>A few Coptic words</title>
          <meta charset=utf-8>
        </head>

        <body>
          <p><span>‚≤°‚≤ô‚≤ü‚≤ü‚≤©</span>
            <span>‚Äòwater‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤°‚≤è‚≤ì</span>
            <span>‚Äòhouse‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤°‚≤£‚≤Å‚≤õ</span>
            <span>‚Äòname‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤ß‚≤£ÃÖ‚≤£‚≤±</span>
            <span>‚Äòqueen‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>œ©‚≤Å</span>
            <span>‚Äòunder‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤°‚≤±‚≤õ‚≤â</span>
            <span>‚Äòstone‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤°œ©‚≤Å‚≤ì</span>
            <span>‚Äòhusband‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤°‚≤õ‚≤ü‚≤©‚≤É</span>
            <span>‚Äògold‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤ß‚≤ô‚≤Å‚≤Å‚≤©</span>
            <span>‚Äòmother‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤Å‚≤õ</span>
            <span>‚Äònot‚Äô</span>
          </p>
        </body>
        </html>

47. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207745727401300018}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .groupStart__56db5 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207745727401300018" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207745727401300018 uid_1 message-content-1207745727401300018 message-accessories-1207745727401300018 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207745727401300018" aria-describedby="uid_3 message-reactions-1207745727401300018"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    
    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1207745727401300018 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/15/2024 12:50 PM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02152024-1250-pm .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1207745727401300018 message-timestamp-1207745727401300018"}

    ::: {#message-content-1207745727401300018 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} In fact, you could also use the following *even worse*
    markup:
        <!doctype html>
        <html>
        <head>
          <title>A few Coptic words</title>
          <meta charset=utf-8>
        </head>
        <body>
        <br>‚≤°‚≤ô‚≤ü‚≤ü‚≤© ‚Äòwater‚Äô
        <br>‚≤°‚≤è‚≤ì ‚Äòhouse‚Äô
        <br>‚≤°‚≤£‚≤Å‚≤õ ‚Äòname‚Äô
        <br>‚≤ß‚≤£ÃÖ‚≤£‚≤± ‚Äòqueen‚Äô
        <br>œ©‚≤Å ‚Äòunder‚Äô
        <br>‚≤°‚≤±‚≤õ‚≤â ‚Äòstone‚Äô
        <br>‚≤°œ©‚≤Å‚≤ì ‚Äòhusband‚Äô
        <br>‚≤°‚≤õ‚≤ü‚≤©‚≤É ‚Äògold‚Äô
        <br>‚≤ß‚≤ô‚≤Å‚≤Å‚≤© ‚Äòmother‚Äô
        <br>‚≤Å‚≤õ ‚Äònot‚Äô
        </body>
        </html>

    Here only the line spacing has shifted a bit, practically
    equivalent. But this is *much* worse than either of the two
    preceding examples, because we are using the `<br>`{.inline} "line
    break" tag to put each word/definition pair on its own line. Seems
    like it should be right, right? Wrong. The [`<br>`{.inline}
    tag](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTML/Element/br "<br> tag

    (https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTML/Element/br)"){.anchor_c8ddc0
    .anchorUnderlineOnHover__78236 rel="noreferrer noopener"
    target="_blank" role="button" tabindex="0"} is *only* for "useful
    for writing a poem or an address, where the division of lines is
    significant." It's a bit subtle, but basically we are concerned here
    that our "words" are not *contained* by tags. The `<br>`{.inline}s
    are just inserted in the flow of text as if they were words
    themselves. Not sure if that makes sense. But when you see
    `<br>`{.inline}s like that, *unless* it's to do with lines in a
    manuscript transcription, say, you should be suspicious.
    :::
    :::

48. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207746740560855141}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207746740560855141" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207745727401300018 uid_1 message-content-1207746740560855141 message-accessories-1207746740560855141 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207746740560855141"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    [*\[*12:54 PM*\]* ]{.latin24CompactTimeStamp__21614
    .timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampVisibleOnHover_e8cc6d .alt__6c563}

    ::: {#message-content-1207746740560855141 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} So much for this being a short post. One last thing.
    Since we've been talking about this containment business, as we said
    above, there's still something else missing: a tag corresponding to
    the *whole list*. You might say "well, the `<body>`{.inline} tag
    contains the list." which is sort of true. But it's more than likely
    that there will be other stuff on our page, like, say, a heading.
    The `<h1>`{.inline} tag means "most important or top-level heading".
    So:
        <!doctype html>
        <html>

        <head>
          <title>A few Coptic words</title>
          <meta charset=utf-8>
        </head>

        <body>
          <h1>A few Coptic words</h1>
          <p><span>‚≤°‚≤ô‚≤ü‚≤ü‚≤©</span>
            <span>‚Äòwater‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤°‚≤è‚≤ì</span>
            <span>‚Äòhouse‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤°‚≤£‚≤Å‚≤õ</span>
            <span>‚Äòname‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤ß‚≤£ÃÖ‚≤£‚≤±</span>
            <span>‚Äòqueen‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>œ©‚≤Å</span>
            <span>‚Äòunder‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤°‚≤±‚≤õ‚≤â</span>
            <span>‚Äòstone‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤°œ©‚≤Å‚≤ì</span>
            <span>‚Äòhusband‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤°‚≤õ‚≤ü‚≤©‚≤É</span>
            <span>‚Äògold‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤ß‚≤ô‚≤Å‚≤Å‚≤©</span>
            <span>‚Äòmother‚Äô</span>
          </p>
          <p><span>‚≤Å‚≤õ</span>
            <span>‚Äònot‚Äô</span>
          </p>
        </body>
        </html> 

    This looks fine, but now it can't be said that the `<body>`{.inline}
    tag "corresponds to" or "represents" the word *list* any more. We
    need another level.
    :::
    :::

    ::: {#message-accessories-1207746740560855141 .container_dbadf5}

49. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207748573391749150}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .groupStart__56db5 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1207748573391749150" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1207748573391749150 uid_1 message-content-1207748573391749150 message-accessories-1207748573391749150 uid_2 message-timestamp-1207748573391749150"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    
    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1207748573391749150 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/15/2024 1:01 PM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02152024-101-pm .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1207748573391749150 message-timestamp-1207748573391749150"}

    ::: {#message-content-1207748573391749150 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false" role="button"
    tabindex="0"} I'm going to wrap this up with the comment that the
    following way to mark up the list is just one way to do it. (The
    most obvious alternative would involve
    [lists](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Learn/HTML/Introduction_to_HTML/HTML_text_fundamentals#lists "lists

    (https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Learn/HTML/Introduction_to_HTML/HTML_text_fundamentals#lists)"){.anchor_c8ddc0
    .anchorUnderlineOnHover__78236 rel="noreferrer noopener"
    target="_blank" role="button" tabindex="0"}. It's by no means
    perfect, but it's definitely more sensible markup than anything
    we've seen so far:
        <!doctype html>
        <html>

        <head>
          <title>A few Coptic words</title>
          <meta charset=utf-8>
        </head>

        <body>
          <div>
            <h1>A few Coptic words</h1>
            <p><span>‚≤°‚≤ô‚≤ü‚≤ü‚≤©</span>
              <span>‚Äòwater‚Äô</span>
            </p>
            <p><span>‚≤°‚≤è‚≤ì</span>
              <span>‚Äòhouse‚Äô</span>
            </p>
            <p><span>‚≤°‚≤£‚≤Å‚≤õ</span>
              <span>‚Äòname‚Äô</span>
            </p>
            <p><span>‚≤ß‚≤£ÃÖ‚≤£‚≤±</span>
              <span>‚Äòqueen‚Äô</span>
            </p>
            <p><span>œ©‚≤Å</span>
              <span>‚Äòunder‚Äô</span>
            </p>
            <p><span>‚≤°‚≤±‚≤õ‚≤â</span>
              <span>‚Äòstone‚Äô</span>
            </p>
            <p><span>‚≤°œ©‚≤Å‚≤ì</span>
              <span>‚Äòhusband‚Äô</span>
            </p>
            <p><span>‚≤°‚≤õ‚≤ü‚≤©‚≤É</span>
              <span>‚Äògold‚Äô</span>
            </p>
            <p><span>‚≤ß‚≤ô‚≤Å‚≤Å‚≤©</span>
              <span>‚Äòmother‚Äô</span>
            </p>
            <p><span>‚≤Å‚≤õ</span>
              <span>‚Äònot‚Äô</span>
            </p>
          </div>
        </body>
        </html>

    As you can see, wrapping the words in a `<div>`{.inline} tag (for
    "division" of a page, which is, like `<span>`{.inline}, a very
    generic) is the only change we have made, and again, the displayed
    content looks almost identical. I'm introducing markup this way
    intentionally because I want you to realize: markup ‚â† display. At
    least, markup and display are not *strictly* equal. Learning to
    control and use the back-and-forth between content and presentation
    is one of the main magical powers of the web, believe it or not. It
    makes the rest of what we will learn possible.
    :::
    :::

    I'm also realizing I should put this stuff into a web page before I
    get too deep into writing chapters, because it would be kind of

59. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1208117129870577666}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .mentioned__58017 .groupStart__56db5 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 .hasReply_febd50 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1208117129870577666" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-reply-context-1208117129870577666 uid_1 message-content-1208117129870577666 uid_2 message-timestamp-1208117129870577666"}
    ::: {#message-reply-context-1208117129870577666 .repliedMessage_e2bf4a aria-label="‚≤Ü‚≤Å‚≤©‚≤ì‚≤á replying to ‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß"}
    ![](https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/187076031075713024/3029fb9e16714df73e7512d1f091feac.webp?size=32){.replyAvatar_cea07c
    .clickable_d866f1}[\@‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99
    .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false"
    role="button" tabindex="0"}

    ::: {.repliedTextPreview__90311 .clickable_d866f1 role="button" tabindex="0"}
    ::: {#message-content-1207746740560855141 .repliedTextContent__75526 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    [![ü™ì](/assets/545eb6c121743df9309c.svg){.emoji aria-label="ü™ì"
    draggable="false" data-type="emoji"
    data-name=":axe:"}]{.emojiContainer__4a804
    .emojiContainerClickable__55a4f aria-expanded="false"} So much for
    this being a short post. One last thing. Since we've been talking
    about this containment business, as we said above, there's still
    something else missing: a tag corresponding to the *whole list*. You
    might say "well, the `<body>`{.inline} tag contains the list." which
    is sort of true. But it's more than likely that there will be other
    stuff on our page, like, say, a heading. The `<h1>`{.inline} tag
    means "most important or top-level heading". So:
    `<!doctype html> <html> <head> <title>A few Coptic words</title> <meta charset=utf-8> </head> <body> <h1>A few Coptic words</h1> <p><span>‚≤°‚≤ô‚≤ü‚≤ü‚≤©</span> <span>‚Äòwater‚Äô</span> </p> <p><span>‚≤°‚≤è‚≤ì</span> <span>‚Äòhouse‚Äô</span> </p> <p><span>‚≤°‚≤£‚≤Å‚≤õ</span> <span>‚Äòname‚Äô</span> </p> <p><span>‚≤ß‚≤£ÃÖ‚≤£‚≤±</span> <span>‚Äòqueen‚Äô</span> </p> <p><span>œ©‚≤Å</span> <span>‚Äòunder‚Äô</span> </p> <p><span>‚≤°‚≤±‚≤õ‚≤â</span> <span>‚Äòstone‚Äô</span> </p> <p><span>‚≤°œ©‚≤Å‚≤ì</span> <span>‚Äòhusband‚Äô</span> </p> <p><span>‚≤°‚≤õ‚≤ü‚≤©‚≤É</span> <span>‚Äògold‚Äô</span> </p> <p><span>‚≤ß‚≤ô‚≤Å‚≤Å‚≤©</span> <span>‚Äòmother‚Äô</span> </p> <p><span>‚≤Å‚≤õ</span> <span>‚Äònot‚Äô</span> </p> </body> </html> `{.inline}
    This looks fine, but now it can't be said that the `<body>`{.inline}
    tag "corresponds to" or "represents" the word *list* any more. We
    need another level.
    :::
    :::

    ![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyBjbGFzcz0icmVwbGllZFRleHRDb250ZW50SWNvbl9fNGRkODIiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIiB4bWxucz0iaHR0cDovL3d3dy53My5vcmcvMjAwMC9zdmciIHdpZHRoPSIyMCIgaGVpZ2h0PSIyMCIgZmlsbD0ibm9uZSIgdmlld2JveD0iMCAwIDI0IDI0Ij48cGF0aCBmaWxsPSJjdXJyZW50Q29sb3IiIGZpbGwtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgZD0iTTIgNWEzIDMgMCAwIDEgMy0zaDE0YTMgMyAwIDAgMSAzIDN2MTRhMyAzIDAgMCAxLTMgM0g1YTMgMyAwIDAgMS0zLTNWNVptMTMuMzUgOC4xMyAzLjUgNC42N2MuMzcuNS4wMiAxLjItLjYgMS4ySDUuODFhLjc1Ljc1IDAgMCAxLS41OS0xLjIybDEuODYtMi4zMmExLjUgMS41IDAgMCAxIDIuMzQgMGwuNS42NCAyLjIzLTIuOTdhMiAyIDAgMCAxIDMuMiAwWk0xMC4yIDUuOThjLjIzLS45MS0uODgtMS41NS0xLjU1LS45YS45My45MyAwIDAgMS0xLjMgMGMtLjY3LS42NS0xLjc4LS4wMS0xLjU1LjlhLjkzLjkzIDAgMCAxLS42NSAxLjEyYy0uOS4yNi0uOSAxLjU0IDAgMS44LjQ4LjE0Ljc3LjYzLjY1IDEuMTItLjIzLjkxLjg4IDEuNTUgMS41NS45YS45My45MyAwIDAgMSAxLjMgMGMuNjcuNjUgMS43OC4wMSAxLjU1LS45YS45My45MyAwIDAgMSAuNjUtMS4xMmMuOS0uMjYuOS0xLjU0IDAtMS44YS45My45MyAwIDAgMS0uNjUtMS4xMloiIGNsaXAtcnVsZT0iZXZlbm9kZCIgY2xhc3M+PC9wYXRoPjwvc3ZnPg==){.repliedTextContentIcon__4dd82}
    :::

    ::: contents_f41bb2
    ![
    ](https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/359461577394618374/e4065d0bd843dc8b280cf3e8ec84f16f.webp?size=160){.avatar__08316
    .clickable_d866f1 aria-hidden="true"}
    ### [[‚≤Ü‚≤Å‚≤©‚≤ì‚≤á]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1208117129870577666 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/16/2024 1:26 PM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤á‚≤Å‚≤©‚≤ì‚≤á-02162024-126-pm .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1208117129870577666 message-timestamp-1208117129870577666" aria-describedby="message-reply-context-1208117129870577666"}

    ::: {#message-content-1208117129870577666 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    So the \<span\> tags within the \<p\> tags look exactly the same on
    the webpage as if you had put \<p\>s within \<p\>, but by
    distinguishing you're expressing that they are at different 'levels'

65. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1208117722114953256}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .groupStart__56db5 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1208117722114953256" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1208117722114953256 uid_1 message-content-1208117722114953256 uid_2 message-timestamp-1208117722114953256"}
    ::: contents_f41bb2
    
    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1208117722114953256 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/16/2024 1:28 PM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02162024-128-pm .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1208117722114953256 message-timestamp-1208117722114953256"}

    ::: {#message-content-1208117722114953256 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    the reason it\'s important to know about the tag hierarchy business
    is that any tag can be styled in any way, and a lot of tutorials
    start people off with things liek `<strong>`{.inline}, and people
    get the wrong idea of "oh, `<strong>`{.inline} means 'bold'", which
    isn't true
    :::
    :::

    ::: {#message-accessories-1208117722114953256 .container_dbadf5}

66. ::: {#chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1208117884799291412}
    ::: {.message__80c10 .cozyMessage__64ce7 .wrapper__09ecc .cozy_f5c119 .zalgo__39311 role="article" list-item-id="chat-messages___chat-messages-1206785883492188170-1208117884799291412" tabindex="-1" aria-setsize="-1" aria-roledescription="Message" aria-labelledby="message-username-1208117722114953256 uid_1 message-content-1208117884799291412 uid_2 message-timestamp-1208117884799291412"}

    by *default* strong is styled as bold. and by *default*
    `<em>`{.inline} is styled as italic. but `<em>`{.inline} means
    "emphasis", and in anotherl naguage for instance it might be
    rendered in a different way.

    ### [[‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß]{.username_d30d99 .desaturateUserColors_b72bd3 .clickable_d866f1 aria-expanded="false" role="button" tabindex="0"}]{#message-username-1208141609141665793 .headerText_f47574}[ *---* 02/16/2024 3:03 PM]{.timestamp_cdbd93 .timestampInline__470e0} {#‚≤°‚≤Å‚≤ß-02162024-303-pm .header__39b23 aria-labelledby="message-username-1208141609141665793 message-timestamp-1208141609141665793" aria-describedby="message-reply-context-1208141609141665793"}

    ::: {#message-content-1208141609141665793 .markup_a7e664 .messageContent__21e69}
    Oh whoops, I didn\'t read your comment carefully, sorry. In fact, a
    `<span>`{.inline} and a `<p>`{.inline} are going to render
    differently for another reason: the `<p>`{.inline} will get its own
    line, and the `<span>`{.inline} will not. Some tags can nest, and
    others cannot. So, you can do
    `<span> grandparent <span> parent <span>child</span></span></span>`{.inline},
    for instance. But oddly enough, you *can't* do that with
    `<p>`{.inline} tags, or at least, you shouldn't, because weird
    things will happen. Another difference between `<p>`{.inline} and
    `<span>`{.inline} is that `<p>`{.inline} gets its own line and
    `<span>`{.inline} does not. These are called "block-level" and
    "inline" tags, respectively. There is a different block-level tag
    does allow nesting, that's `<div>`{.inline}. So
    `<div>this <div> is also <div>okay.</div></div></div>`{.inline}.
    :::
    :::

    ::: {#message-accessories-1208141609141665793 .container_dbadf5}
    :::
    :::
    :::
